1. [measurement_frequency_definition]
Topic: measurement
Difficulty: beginner
Outline: A-1 (A)
Question: Which concept is being described as the RBT counts each instance of a target behavior during the observation period.
Options:
  A) Work sample collection
  B) Observable terms
  C) Components of a behavior graph
  D) Frequency recording
Correct answer: D) Frequency recording
Explanation: Frequency recording is used when the team needs an exact count of how many times behavior happened.

Options:
  A) To recognize the danger of basing decisions on poor-quality data.
  B) To have the recording tool ready so no data are missed once the session begins.

40. [behavior_dra_definition]
Topic: behavior_reduction
Difficulty: beginner
Outline: D-3 (D)
Question: Which concept is being described as reinforcement is delivered for a desired alternative or incompatible response while problem behavior is not reinforced.
Options:
  A) Differential reinforcement
  B) Abolishing operation
  C) Antecedent intervention
  D) Attention-maintained replacement response
Correct answer: A) Differential reinforcement
Explanation: Differential reinforcement builds a better response while reducing reinforcement for the problem behavior.

Difficulty: intermediate

  B) Learner response in DTT
  C) Data collection system in a SAP
  D) Maintenance programming
Correct answer: D) Maintenance programming
Explanation: Maintenance ensures mastered skills continue over time instead of dropping once formal teaching stops.

Outline: C-7 (C)

Options:
  A) Stimulus control transfer
  B) Total task chaining
  C) Reinforcement magnitude
  D) Avoiding prompt dependency
Correct answer: A) Stimulus control transfer
Explanation: Stimulus control transfer is the goal of effective prompt fading and independence-building.

  C) To assess whether two observers measured the same amount of time for the same behavioral episode.
  D) To convert a permanent product into a numerical score that reflects how accurately the skill was performed.
Correct answer: A) To recognize that interval-based systems sacrifice precision for practicality.
Explanation: Understanding this limitation helps the RBT report data correctly and communicate to the supervisor when the measure may be underestimating the behavior. The main goal is to recognize that interval-based systems sacrifice precision for practicality.

  D) Stimulus sampling in preference assessment

Explanation: Sampling across stimulus categories ensures the team does not overlook potential reinforcers that the learner has not yet had a chance to show preference for.

640. [skill_reinforcement_immediacy_definition]

  C) Comparing chaining methods
  D) Reinforcement immediacy

  B) Token exchange procedure
  C) Conditioned reinforcer
  D) Positive reinforcement

Options:
  A) To ensure that correct responses are reinforced and errors are addressed consistently.
  B) To maintain a learned behavior while making it more resistant to extinction by reducing reinforcement frequency gradually.
  C) To promote independence by making natural environmental cues — rather than staff instructions — the trigger for the behavior.
  D) To recognize how two different NET strategies can be used flexibly depending on what naturally occurs.
Correct answer: A) To ensure that correct responses are reinforced and errors are addressed consistently.
Explanation: Consistent consequence delivery teaches the learner which responses produce reinforcement and which require correction. The main goal is to ensure that correct responses are reinforced and errors are addressed consistently.

---

661. [skill_dtt_intertrial_interval_definition]
Topic: skill_acquisition
Difficulty: beginner
Outline: C-3 (C)
Question: Which concept is being described as the intertrial interval is the brief pause between one trial ending and the next SD being delivered.
Options:
  A) Introducing targets in discrimination training
  B) Intertrial interval (ITI)
  C) Positive reinforcement
  D) Model prompt
Correct answer: B) Intertrial interval (ITI)
Explanation: A consistent intertrial interval separates trials clearly and helps prevent position biases or prompt dependency that can develop without a pause.

---

667. [skill_dtt_massed_practice_definition]

  B) Variable-interval schedule
  C) Massed vs. distributed practice in DTT
  D) Stimulus generalization
Correct answer: C) Massed vs. distributed practice in DTT

676. [skill_dtt_trial_pacing_definition]

  C) Comparing chaining methods
  D) Error correction in discrimination training
Correct answer: C) Comparing chaining methods
Explanation: Each chaining method has different advantages; the choice depends on the nature of the skill, the learner's abilities, and the clinical judgment of the supervisor.

712. [skill_discriminative_stimulus_sd_definition]

  D) Pre-session program review

727. [skill_stimulus_control_definition_definition]

Difficulty: intermediate
Outline: C-7 (C)
Question: In constant time delay, the RBT always waits 5 seconds before prompting; in progressive time delay, the wait starts at 0 seconds and increases by 1 second each session. Which concept is the best match?
Options:
  A) Constant vs. progressive time delay
  B) Backward chaining
  C) Response prompt
  D) Pre-session data review
Correct answer: A) Constant vs. progressive time delay
Explanation: Both procedures allow the learner to respond independently within the delay interval; choosing between them depends on the learner's history and the supervisor's preference.

---

Difficulty: intermediate
Outline: C-7 (C)
Question: What is the main goal of Constant vs. progressive time delay?

  A) To reinforce responding after changing time intervals.
  B) To address multiple skill areas within one session efficiently.
  C) To ensure the contingency between the response and the reinforcer is clear to the learner.
  D) To understand how different time delay procedures transfer stimulus control from the prompt to the natural SD.
Correct answer: D) To understand how different time delay procedures transfer stimulus control from the prompt to the natural SD.

The main goal is to understand how different time delay procedures transfer stimulus control from the prompt to the natural sd.

748. [skill_stimulus_control_transfer_definition]
Topic: skill_acquisition
Difficulty: beginner
Outline: C-7 (C)
Question: Which concept is being described as stimulus control is transferred when a behavior originally controlled by a prompt shifts to being controlled by the natural antecedent stimulus.
Options:
  A) Stimulus control transfer
  B) Reinforcement magnitude
  C) Total task chaining
  D) Avoiding prompt dependency
Correct answer: A) Stimulus control transfer
Explanation: Successful stimulus control transfer is the goal of all prompt fading — the natural SD comes to control the behavior without the help of the prompt.

778. [skill_shaping_step_advancement_definition]

Difficulty: intermediate
Outline: C-10 (C)

  B) Stimulus prompt fading
  C) Token exchange procedure
  D) Model prompt

790. [skill_shaping_regression_definition]
Topic: skill_acquisition
Difficulty: intermediate
Outline: C-10 (C)
Question: Which concept is being described as if the learner consistently fails to meet the current criterion, the RBT returns to the previous step to re-establish successful responding before advancing again.
Options:
  A) Behavioral objective in a SAP
  B) Going back a step in shaping
  C) Multiple exemplar training
  D) Step size in shaping
Correct answer: B) Going back a step in shaping
Explanation: Going back a step is not a failure — it allows the learner to regain momentum and success before attempting the more challenging approximation again.

808. [skill_token_ratio_definition]
Topic: skill_acquisition
Difficulty: intermediate
Outline: C-11 (C)

  A) Maintenance probe
  B) Stimulus prompt
  C) Behavioral objective in a SAP
  D) Token-to-backup ratio
Correct answer: D) Token-to-backup ratio
Explanation: A ratio that is too high leads to frustration; a ratio that is too low reduces session productivity. The ratio should be adjusted as the learner's performance develops.

820. [behavior_function_vs_topography_definition]
Topic: behavior_reduction
Difficulty: beginner
Outline: D-1 (D)
Question: Which concept is being described as the topography of a behavior is what it looks like, while the function is the consequence that maintains it; two behaviors can look the same but serve different functions.
Options:
  A) Extinction side effects
  B) Function vs. topography of behavior
  C) Differential reinforcement of alternative behavior
  D) Choice making
Correct answer: B) Function vs. topography of behavior
Explanation: Intervening based on topography alone without understanding function can result in a plan that is ineffective or that accidentally strengthens the behavior.

823. [behavior_environment_modification_definition]

829. [behavior_transition_warning_definition]

832. [behavior_task_modification_definition]
Topic: behavior_reduction
Difficulty: intermediate
Outline: D-2 (D)

  B) Differential reinforcement of reduced rates
  C) De-escalation strategies
  D) Task modification

Explanation: Task modification should be done only as described in the behavior plan; arbitrary changes to tasks can inadvertently reinforce avoidance if not managed carefully.

Options:
  A) To interrupt problem behavior and guide the learner to a more appropriate response.
  B) To reduce the motivation to escape or avoid demands by making them more manageable.
  C) To reduce the likelihood of problem behavior by changing conditions in advance.
  D) To describe events that alter reinforcer value and related behavior.
Correct answer: B) To reduce the motivation to escape or avoid demands by making them more manageable.
Explanation: Task modification should be done only as described in the behavior plan; arbitrary changes to tasks can inadvertently reinforce avoidance if not managed carefully. The main goal is to reduce the motivation to escape or avoid demands by making them more manageable.

---

835. [behavior_extinction_consistency_definition]
Topic: behavior_reduction
Difficulty: beginner
Outline: D-4 (D)
Question: Which concept is being described as extinction must be applied every time the target behavior occurs — intermittent application can accidentally strengthen the behavior.
Options:
  A) Replacement behavior in a BRP
  B) Tangible extinction
  C) Consistency in extinction
  D) Escape-maintained replacement response
Correct answer: C) Consistency in extinction
Explanation: Consistent implementation of extinction is essential; even occasional reinforcement of a behavior during extinction can dramatically prolong it.

---

  A) Escape-maintained replacement response
  B) Consistency in extinction
  C) Replacement behavior in a BRP
  D) Tangible extinction
Correct answer: B) Consistency in extinction
Explanation: Consistent implementation of extinction is essential; even occasional reinforcement of a behavior during extinction can dramatically prolong it.

Difficulty: beginner
Outline: D-4 (D)

  B) To ensure the intervention addresses the actual reason the behavior persists.
  C) To recognize the temporary worsening that can happen when extinction first starts.
  D) To reinforce periods in which the problem behavior does not occur.

838. [behavior_extinction_burst_management_definition]
Topic: behavior_reduction
Difficulty: intermediate
Outline: D-6 (D)

Options:
  A) Redirection
  B) Notifying the supervisor during a crisis
  C) Functional communication training
  D) Managing an extinction burst
Correct answer: D) Managing an extinction burst
Explanation: The RBT should be prepared for an extinction burst and stay consistent; stopping extinction during a burst accidentally reinforces the escalated behavior.

841. [behavior_spontaneous_recovery_definition]
Topic: behavior_reduction
Difficulty: intermediate
Outline: D-6 (D)
Question: Which concept is being described as a previously extinguished behavior may briefly reappear after a period without the behavior, even though extinction is still in place.
Options:
  A) Differential reinforcement of reduced rates
  B) Replacement behavior in a BRP
  C) Crisis plan section of a BRP
  D) Spontaneous recovery
Correct answer: D) Spontaneous recovery
Explanation: Spontaneous recovery is temporary if extinction is continued consistently; giving in when the behavior reappears can restart the reinforcement history.

  A) Safety escalation
  B) Following the treatment plan
  C) Truthful representation
  D) Caregiver behavior support as authorized
Correct answer: D) Caregiver behavior support as authorized
Explanation: Caregiver training is directed and authorized by the supervisor; the RBT should not independently develop or modify what is taught to the caregiver.

949. [skill_graduated_guidance_definition]

  B) Stimulus control transfer
  C) Graduated guidance
  D) Model prompt

  D) To protect the learner and the RBT from preventable harm caused by unsafe conditions.
Correct answer: D) To protect the learner and the RBT from preventable harm caused by unsafe conditions.
Explanation: Reporting environmental hazards is part of the RBT's responsibility to maintain a safe treatment environment and protect the learner's wellbeing. The main goal is to protect the learner and the rbt from preventable harm caused by unsafe conditions.
